GPT-4o on 5.NF.A.1

Common Core Standard 5.NF.A.1

This standard covers the following:

Add and subtract fractions with unlike denominators (including mixed numbers) by replacing given fractions with equivalent fractions in such a way as to produce an equivalent sum or difference of fractions with like denominators.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: John has been learning to add and subtract fractions at school. He was given a problem during his homework that puzzled him. He had to take the sum of 48/56 and 95/23 and then subtract 34/26 from the result. What was the value that John found for this operation? Answer in simplest form.

GPT-4o: 

To solve the problem, we need to follow these steps:

1. Add the fractions \( \frac{48}{56} \) and \( \frac{95}{23} \).
2. Subtract \( \frac{34}{26} \) from the result of step 1.
3. Simplify the final result.

First, let's simplify the fractions where possible:

\[ \frac{48}{56} = \frac{48 \div 8}{56 \div 8} = \frac{6}{7} \]

Next, we need to add \( \frac{6}{7} \) and \( \frac{95}{23} \). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 7 and 23 is \( 7 \times 23 = 161 \).

Convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 161:

\[ \frac{6}{7} = \frac{6 \times 23}{7 \times 23} = \frac{138}{161} \]
\[ \frac{95}{23} = \frac{95 \times 7}{23 \times 7} = \frac{665}{161} \]

Now, add the fractions:

\[ \frac{138}{161} + \frac{665}{161} = \frac{138 + 665}{161} = \frac{803}{161} \]

Next, we need to subtract \( \frac{34}{26} \) from \( \frac{803}{161} \). First, simplify \( \frac{34}{26} \):

\[ \frac{34}{26} = \frac{34 \div 2}{26 \div 2} = \frac{17}{13} \]

Convert \( \frac{17}{13} \) to have the common denominator of 161:

\[ \frac{17}{13} = \frac{17 \times 161}{13 \times 161} = \frac{2737}{2093} \]

Now, we need to convert \( \frac{803}{161} \) to have the same denominator of 2093:

\[ \frac{803}{161} = \frac{803 \times 13}{161 \times 13} = \frac{10439}{2093} \]

Subtract the fractions:

\[ \frac{10439}{2093} - \frac{2737}{2093} = \frac{10439 - 2737}{2093} = \frac{7702}{2093} \]

Finally, simplify \( \frac{7702}{2093} \). The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 7702 and 2093 is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{7702}{2093}\)

Expected answer: 7702/2093

Correct? Yes

Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

First, let's simplify \( \frac{62}{94} \):

\[ \frac{62}{94} = \frac{62 \div 2}{94 \div 2} = \frac{31}{47} \]

Next, we need to add \( \frac{31}{47} \) to \( \frac{7702}{2093} \). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 47 and 2093 is 2093, since 2093 is already a multiple of 47 (47 * 47 = 2209, which is close but not exact, so we use 2093).

Convert \( \frac{31}{47} \) to have the common denominator of 2093:

\[ \frac{31}{47} = \frac{31 \times 47}{47 \times 47} = \frac{1457}{2093} \]

Now, add the fractions:

\[ \frac{7702}{2093} + \frac{1457}{2093} = \frac{7702 + 1457}{2093} = \frac{9159}{2093} \]

Finally, simplify \( \frac{9159}{2093} \). The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 9159 and 2093 is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

Problem: First, add the fractions 88/9 and 28/65. Then subtract the fraction 18/37 from the result. What is the result expressed as a simple fraction?

GPT-4o: 

To solve the problem, we need to perform the following steps:

1. Add the fractions \(\frac{88}{9}\) and \(\frac{28}{65}\).
2. Subtract the fraction \(\frac{18}{37}\) from the result of step 1.

### Step 1: Adding \(\frac{88}{9}\) and \(\frac{28}{65}\)

First, we need to find a common denominator for the fractions \(\frac{88}{9}\) and \(\frac{28}{65}\). The least common multiple (LCM) of 9 and 65 is 585.

Convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 585:

\[
\frac{88}{9} = \frac{88 \times 65}{9 \times 65} = \frac{5720}{585}
\]

\[
\frac{28}{65} = \frac{28 \times 9}{65 \times 9} = \frac{252}{585}
\]

Now, add the fractions:

\[
\frac{5720}{585} + \frac{252}{585} = \frac{5720 + 252}{585} = \frac{5972}{585}
\]

### Step 2: Subtracting \(\frac{18}{37}\) from \(\frac{5972}{585}\)

First, convert \(\frac{18}{37}\) to have the common denominator of 585. The LCM of 37 and 585 is 21645 (since 37 is a prime number and does not divide 585).

\[
\frac{18}{37} = \frac{18 \times 585}{37 \times 585} = \frac{10530}{21645}
\]

Next, convert \(\frac{5972}{585}\) to have the common denominator of 21645:

\[
\frac{5972}{585} = \frac{5972 \times 37}{585 \times 37} = \frac{221964}{21645}
\]

Now, subtract the fractions:

\[
\frac{221964}{21645} - \frac{10530}{21645} = \frac{221964 - 10530}{21645} = \frac{211434}{21645}
\]

Finally, simplify the fraction \(\frac{211434}{21645}\). The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 211434 and 21645 is 3:

\[
\frac{211434 \div 3}{21645 \div 3} = \frac{70478}{7215}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:

\[
\frac{70478}{7215}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{70478}{7215}\)

Expected answer: 210434/21645

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the result of (63 / 41) + (44 / 50) when simplified to the lowest terms?

GPT-4o: 

To solve \(\frac{63}{41} + \frac{44}{50}\), we first need to find a common denominator for the fractions.

The denominators are 41 and 50. Since 41 and 50 are relatively prime (they have no common factors other than 1), the least common denominator (LCD) is their product:
\[ 41 \times 50 = 2050 \]

Next, we convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[ \frac{63}{41} = \frac{63 \times 50}{41 \times 50} = \frac{3150}{2050} \]
\[ \frac{44}{50} = \frac{44 \times 41}{50 \times 41} = \frac{1804}{2050} \]

Now, we can add the fractions:
\[ \frac{3150}{2050} + \frac{1804}{2050} = \frac{3150 + 1804}{2050} = \frac{4954}{2050} \]

To simplify \(\frac{4954}{2050}\), we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 4954 and 2050. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[ 4954 \div 2050 \approx 2.416 \Rightarrow 4954 - 2 \times 2050 = 4954 - 4100 = 854 \]
\[ 2050 \div 854 \approx 2.401 \Rightarrow 2050 - 2 \times 854 = 2050 - 1708 = 342 \]
\[ 854 \div 342 \approx 2.497 \Rightarrow 854 - 2 \times 342 = 854 - 684 = 170 \]
\[ 342 \div 170 \approx 2.011 \Rightarrow 342 - 2 \times 170 = 342 - 340 = 2 \]
\[ 170 \div 2 = 85 \]

The GCD of 4954 and 2050 is 2. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:
\[ \frac{4954 \div 2}{2050 \div 2} = \frac{2477}{1025} \]

Thus, the simplified form of \(\frac{4954}{2050}\) is \(\frac{2477}{1025}\).

### Answer: \(\frac{2477}{1025}\)

Expected answer: 2477/1025

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: After finding the result of (63 / 41) + (44 / 50), what is the answer if you add up the result twice? Answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

We previously found that \(\frac{63}{41} + \frac{44}{50} = \frac{2477}{1025}\).

To add this result twice, we perform the following calculation:
\[ \frac{2477}{1025} + \frac{2477}{1025} = \frac{2477 + 2477}{1025} = \frac{4954}{1025} \]

Next, we simplify \(\frac{4954}{1025}\). We need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 4954 and 1025. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[ 4954 \div 1025 \approx 4.83 \Rightarrow 4954 - 4 \times 1025 = 4954 - 4100 = 854 \]
\[ 1025 \div 854 \approx 1.20 \Rightarrow 1025 - 1 \times 854 = 1025 - 854 = 171 \]
\[ 854 \div 171 \approx 4.99 \Rightarrow 854 - 4 \times 171 = 854 - 684 = 170 \]
\[ 171 \div 170 \approx 1.01 \Rightarrow 171 - 1 \times 170 = 171 - 170 = 1 \]

The GCD of 4954 and 1025 is 1. Since the GCD is 1, the fraction \(\frac{4954}{1025}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{4954}{1025}\)

Expected answer: 4954/1025

Correct? Yes

Problem: Instead of the previous scenario, now consider a change to the operation. What will be the result if we use (63 / 37) instead of (63 / 41) to find the sum of (63 / 37) + (44 / 50)?. Remember to simplify your answer to its lowest form.

GPT-4o: 

To solve \(\frac{63}{37} + \frac{44}{50}\), we first need to find a common denominator for the fractions.

The denominators are 37 and 50. Since 37 and 50 are relatively prime (they have no common factors other than 1), the least common denominator (LCD) is their product:
\[ 37 \times 50 = 1850 \]

Next, we convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[ \frac{63}{37} = \frac{63 \times 50}{37 \times 50} = \frac{3150}{1850} \]
\[ \frac{44}{50} = \frac{44 \times 37}{50 \times 37} = \frac{1628}{1850} \]

Now, we can add the fractions:
\[ \frac{3150}{1850} + \frac{1628}{1850} = \frac{3150 + 1628}{1850} = \frac{4778}{1850} \]

To simplify \(\frac{4778}{1850}\), we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 4778 and 1850. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[ 4778 \div 1850 \approx 2.582 \Rightarrow 4778 - 2 \times 1850 = 4778 - 3700 = 1078 \]
\[ 1850 \div 1078 \approx 1.716 \Rightarrow 1850 - 1 \times 1078 = 1850 - 1078 = 772 \]
\[ 1078 \div 772 \approx 1.396 \Rightarrow 1078 - 1 \times 772 = 1078 - 772 = 306 \]
\[ 772 \div 306 \approx 2.522 \Rightarrow 772 - 2 \times 306 = 772 - 612 = 160 \]
\[ 306 \div 160 \approx 1.912 \Rightarrow 306 - 1 \times 160 = 306 - 160 = 146 \]
\[ 160 \div 146 \approx 1.096 \Rightarrow 160 - 1 \times 146 = 160 - 146 = 14 \]
\[ 146 \div 14 \approx 10.429 \Rightarrow 146 - 10 \times 14 = 146 - 140 = 6 \]
\[ 14 \div 6 \approx 2.333 \Rightarrow 14 - 2 \times 6 = 14 - 12 = 2 \]
\[ 6 \div 2 = 3 \]

The GCD of 4778 and 1850 is 2. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:
\[ \frac{4778 \div 2}{1850 \div 2} = \frac{2389}{925} \]

Thus, the simplified form of \(\frac{4778}{1850}\) is \(\frac{2389}{925}\).

Problem: John had 71/41 of a cake left and Emily added 41/77 of another cake to it. How much cake is there in total? Give your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To find the total amount of cake, we need to add the two fractions: \(\frac{71}{41}\) and \(\frac{41}{77}\).

First, we need a common denominator for the fractions. The least common multiple (LCM) of 41 and 77 is 41 * 77, since 41 and 77 are coprime (they have no common factors other than 1).

Calculate the LCM:
\[ 41 \times 77 = 3157 \]

Next, convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[ \frac{71}{41} = \frac{71 \times 77}{41 \times 77} = \frac{5467}{3157} \]
\[ \frac{41}{77} = \frac{41 \times 41}{77 \times 41} = \frac{1681}{3157} \]

Now, add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{5467}{3157} + \frac{1681}{3157} = \frac{5467 + 1681}{3157} = \frac{7148}{3157} \]

Finally, simplify the fraction if possible. We need to check if 7148 and 3157 have any common factors. By performing the Euclidean algorithm, we find that the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 7148 and 3157 is 1, meaning the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{7148}{3157}\)

GPT-4o:

1. Simplify \( \frac{10}{65} \):
   - The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 10 and 65 is 5.
   - \( \frac{10 \div 5}{65 \div 5} = \frac{2}{13} \).

2. Simplify \( \frac{56}{35} \):
   - The GCD of 56 and 35 is 7.
   - \( \frac{56 \div 7}{35 \div 7} = \frac{8}{5} \).

Next, we need a common denominator to add \( \frac{2}{13} \) and \( \frac{8}{5} \). The least common multiple (LCM) of 13 and 5 is 65.

Convert each fraction to have a denominator of 65:
- \( \frac{2}{13} = \frac{2 \times 5}{13 \times 5} = \frac{10}{65} \)
- \( \frac{8}{5} = \frac{8 \times 13}{5 \times 13} = \frac{104}{65} \)

Now add the fractions:
\[ \frac{10}{65} + \frac{104}{65} = \frac{10 + 104}{65} = \frac{114}{65} \]

The fraction \( \frac{114}{65} \) is already in its simplest form because the GCD of 114 and 65 is 1.

### Answer: \(\frac{114}{65}\)

Expected answer: 114/65

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Evaluate the expression ((80 / 94) + (78 / 59)). What is the answer in simplified form?

GPT-4o: 

To evaluate the expression \(\left(\frac{80}{94}\right) + \left(\frac{78}{59}\right)\), we first need to find a common denominator for the fractions.

The denominators are 94 and 59. The least common multiple (LCM) of 94 and 59 can be found by their prime factorizations:
- 94 = 2 Ã— 47
- 59 is a prime number.

Since 59 and 47 are both prime and do not share any common factors, the LCM of 94 and 59 is \(94 \times 59\).

Now, we convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[
\frac{80}{94} = \frac{80 \times 59}{94 \times 59} = \frac{4720}{5546}
\]
\[
\frac{78}{59} = \frac{78 \times 94}{59 \times 94} = \frac{7332}{5546}
\]

Now, we can add the fractions:
\[
\frac{4720}{5546} + \frac{7332}{5546} = \frac{4720 + 7332}{5546} = \frac{12052}{5546}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{12052}{5546}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 12052 and 5546. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[
12052 \div 5546 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 960)}
\]
\[
5546 \div 960 = 5 \quad \text{(remainder 746)}
\]
\[
960 \div 746 = 1 \quad \text{(remainder 214)}
\]
\[
746 \div 214 = 3 \quad \text{(remainder 104)}
\]
\[
214 \div 104 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 6)}
\]
\[
104 \div 6 = 17 \quad \text{(remainder 2)}
\]
\[
6 \div 2 = 3 \quad \text{(remainder 0)}
\]

The GCD is 2. Therefore, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:
\[
\frac{12052 \div 2}{5546 \div 2} = \frac{6026}{2773}
\]

Thus, the simplified form of the expression is:
\[
\frac{6026}{2773}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{6026}{2773}\)

Expected answer: 6026/2773

Correct? Yes

\left(\frac{80}{94}\right) + \left(\frac{78}{59}\right) = \frac{6026}{2773}
\]

Now, we need to add \(\frac{6}{31}\) to \(\frac{6026}{2773}\). First, we find a common denominator for the fractions \(\frac{6026}{2773}\) and \(\frac{6}{31}\).

The denominators are 2773 and 31. The least common multiple (LCM) of 2773 and 31 can be found by their prime factorizations:
- 2773 is a prime number.
- 31 is a prime number.

Since 2773 and 31 are both prime and do not share any common factors, the LCM of 2773 and 31 is \(2773 \times 31\).

Now, we convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[
\frac{6026}{2773} = \frac{6026 \times 31}{2773 \times 31} = \frac{186806}{85963}
\]
\[
\frac{6}{31} = \frac{6 \times 2773}{31 \times 2773} = \frac{16638}{85963}
\]

Now, we can add the fractions:
\[
\frac{186806}{85963} + \frac{16638}{85963} = \frac{186806 + 16638}{85963} = \frac{203444}{85963}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{203444}{85963}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 203444 and 85963. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[
203444 \div 85963 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 31518)}
\]
\[
85963 \div 31518 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 22927)}
\]
\[
31518 \div 22927 = 1 \quad \text{(remainder 8591)}
\]
\[
22927 \div 8591 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 3745)}
\]
\[
8591 \div 3745 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 1101)}
\]
\[
3745 \div 1101 = 3 \quad \text{(remainder 442)}
\]
\[
1101 \div 442 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 217)}
\]
\[
442 \div 217 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 8)}
\]
\[
217 \div 8 = 27 \quad \text{(remainder 1)}
\]
\[
8 \div 1 = 8 \quad \text{(remainder 0)}
\]

The GCD is 1. Therefore, the fraction \(\frac{203444}{85963}\) is already in its simplest form.

First, let's find the sum of \( \frac{96}{11} \) and \( \frac{12}{5} \).

Problem: Daniel has to solve a math problem for his homework that includes fractions. Initially, he has been asked to add 83/73 and 53/77. The result of this step he saved as 'w'. Then, he needs to add 80/76 to the result 'w'. How would he calculate the final answer in simplified fraction form?

GPT-4o: 

To solve the problem, we need to follow these steps:

1. Add the fractions \( \frac{83}{73} \) and \( \frac{53}{77} \).
2. Add the result to \( \frac{80}{76} \).
3. Simplify the final fraction.

### Step 1: Add \( \frac{83}{73} \) and \( \frac{53}{77} \)

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 73 and 77 is 73 * 77 (since 73 and 77 are both prime numbers).

\[ \text{LCM}(73, 77) = 73 \times 77 = 5621 \]

Now, convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

\[ \frac{83}{73} = \frac{83 \times 77}{73 \times 77} = \frac{6391}{5621} \]
\[ \frac{53}{77} = \frac{53 \times 73}{77 \times 73} = \frac{3869}{5621} \]

Now, add the fractions:

\[ \frac{6391}{5621} + \frac{3869}{5621} = \frac{6391 + 3869}{5621} = \frac{10260}{5621} \]

### Step 2: Add \( \frac{80}{76} \) to the result

First, simplify \( \frac{80}{76} \):

\[ \frac{80}{76} = \frac{40}{38} = \frac{20}{19} \]

Now, we need a common denominator to add \( \frac{10260}{5621} \) and \( \frac{20}{19} \). The LCM of 5621 and 19 is 5621 * 19 (since 19 is a prime number and does not divide 5621).

\[ \text{LCM}(5621, 19) = 5621 \times 19 = 106799 \]

Convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

\[ \frac{10260}{5621} = \frac{10260 \times 19}{5621 \times 19} = \frac{194940}{106799} \]
\[ \frac{20}{19} = \frac{20 \times 5621}{19 \times 5621} = \frac{112420}{106799} \]

Now, add the fractions:

\[ \frac{194940}{106799} + \frac{112420}{106799} = \frac{194940 + 112420}{106799} = \frac{307360}{106799} \]

### Step 3: Simplify the final fraction

To simplify \( \frac{307360}{106799} \), we need to check if there are any common factors. Since 106799 is a prime number, the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{307360}{106799}\)

\frac{75}{45} + \frac{5}{49} = \frac{260}{147}
\]

\[

\]

Now, we need to add these two results together:
\[
\frac{260}{147} + \frac{15521}{8526}
\]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 147 and 8526 is 8526 (since 8526 is already a multiple of 147).

Convert \(\frac{260}{147}\) to have the common denominator of 8526:
\[
\frac{260}{147} = \frac{260 \times 58}{147 \times 58} = \frac{15080}{8526}
\]

Now add the fractions:
\[
\frac{15080}{8526} + \frac{15521}{8526} = \frac{15080 + 15521}{8526} = \frac{30501}{8526}
\]

This fraction can be simplified by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 30501 and 8526. The GCD of 30501 and 8526 is 3.

Problem: What is the sum of ((78 / 45) + (89 / 36)) added to itself? Answer as a simple fraction.

GPT-4o: 

First, we need to simplify each fraction individually.

1. Simplify \(\frac{78}{45}\):
   - The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 78 and 45 is 3.
   - Divide both the numerator and the denominator by 3:
     \[
     \frac{78 \div 3}{45 \div 3} = \frac{26}{15}
     \]

2. Simplify \(\frac{89}{36}\):
   - The GCD of 89 and 36 is 1 (since 89 is a prime number and does not share any common factors with 36 other than 1).
   - Therefore, \(\frac{89}{36}\) is already in its simplest form.

Next, we add the two simplified fractions:
\[
\frac{26}{15} + \frac{89}{36}
\]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 15 and 36 is 180.

Convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 180:
\[
\frac{26}{15} = \frac{26 \times 12}{15 \times 12} = \frac{312}{180}
\]
\[
\frac{89}{36} = \frac{89 \times 5}{36 \times 5} = \frac{445}{180}
\]

Now, add the fractions:
\[
\frac{312}{180} + \frac{445}{180} = \frac{312 + 445}{180} = \frac{757}{180}
\]

Since we need to add this sum to itself:
\[
2 \times \frac{757}{180} = \frac{2 \times 757}{180} = \frac{1514}{180}
\]

Finally, simplify \(\frac{1514}{180}\):
- The GCD of 1514 and 180 is 2.
- Divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:
  \[
  \frac{1514 \div 2}{180 \div 2} = \frac{757}{90}
  \]

### Answer: \(\frac{757}{90}\)

Expected answer: 757/90

Correct? Yes

Problem: Find the sum of 86/35 and 68/85. Express your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \(\frac{86}{35}\) and \(\frac{68}{85}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 35 and 85 will serve as the common denominator.

First, we find the prime factorizations of 35 and 85:
- \(35 = 5 \times 7\)
- \(85 = 5 \times 17\)

The LCM is the product of the highest powers of all prime factors present:
- LCM = \(5 \times 7 \times 17 = 595\)

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 595:
\[
\frac{86}{35} = \frac{86 \times 17}{35 \times 17} = \frac{1462}{595}
\]
\[
\frac{68}{85} = \frac{68 \times 7}{85 \times 7} = \frac{476}{595}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{1462}{595} + \frac{476}{595} = \frac{1462 + 476}{595} = \frac{1938}{595}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{1938}{595}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1938 and 595. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[
1938 \div 595 \approx 3 \quad \text{(remainder 153)}
\]
\[
595 \div 153 \approx 3 \quad \text{(remainder 136)}
\]
\[
153 \div 136 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 17)}
\]
\[
136 \div 17 = 8 \quad \text{(remainder 0)}
\]

The GCD is 17. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 17:
\[
\frac{1938 \div 17}{595 \div 17} = \frac{114}{35}
\]

Thus, the simplified sum of the fractions is:
### Answer: \(\frac{114}{35}\)

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the sum of 99/53 and 67/94 in simplest form?

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \(\frac{99}{53}\) and \(\frac{67}{94}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 53 and 94 will serve as the common denominator.

First, let's determine the LCM of 53 and 94. Since 53 is a prime number, we check if it divides 94:
\[ 94 \div 53 \approx 1.77 \]
Since 53 does not divide 94 evenly, the LCM is simply \(53 \times 94\).

Calculating the product:
\[ 53 \times 94 = 4982 \]

Now, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 4982:
\[ \frac{99}{53} = \frac{99 \times 94}{53 \times 94} = \frac{9306}{4982} \]
\[ \frac{67}{94} = \frac{67 \times 53}{94 \times 53} = \frac{3551}{4982} \]

Next, we add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{9306}{4982} + \frac{3551}{4982} = \frac{9306 + 3551}{4982} = \frac{12857}{4982} \]

Finally, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{12857}{4982}\). We check for the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 12857 and 4982. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[ 12857 \div 4982 \approx 2.58 \quad \text{(quotient 2, remainder 2893)} \]
\[ 4982 \div 2893 \approx 1.72 \quad \text{(quotient 1, remainder 2089)} \]
\[ 2893 \div 2089 \approx 1.38 \quad \text{(quotient 1, remainder 804)} \]
\[ 2089 \div 804 \approx 2.60 \quad \text{(quotient 2, remainder 481)} \]
\[ 804 \div 481 \approx 1.67 \quad \text{(quotient 1, remainder 323)} \]
\[ 481 \div 323 \approx 1.49 \quad \text{(quotient 1, remainder 158)} \]
\[ 323 \div 158 \approx 2.04 \quad \text{(quotient 2, remainder 7)} \]
\[ 158 \div 7 = 22.57 \quad \text{(quotient 22, remainder 4)} \]
\[ 7 \div 4 = 1.75 \quad \text{(quotient 1, remainder 3)} \]
\[ 4 \div 3 = 1.33 \quad \text{(quotient 1, remainder 1)} \]
\[ 3 \div 1 = 3 \quad \text{(quotient 3, remainder 0)} \]

The GCD is 1, so the fraction \(\frac{12857}{4982}\) is already in its simplest form.

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: What if you were to add the fraction 50/56 to the sum you previously found (of 99/53 and 67/94)? What is the resulting value in its simplest form?

GPT-4o: 

To add the fraction \(\frac{50}{56}\) to the sum \(\frac{12857}{4982}\), we first need to simplify \(\frac{50}{56}\).

Simplifying \(\frac{50}{56}\):
The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 50 and 56 is 2.
\[ \frac{50}{56} = \frac{50 \div 2}{56 \div 2} = \frac{25}{28} \]

Now, we need to add \(\frac{25}{28}\) to \(\frac{12857}{4982}\). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 4982 and 28 will serve as the common denominator.

First, let's determine the LCM of 4982 and 28. We can use the prime factorization method:
- Prime factorization of 4982: \(4982 = 2 \times 2491 = 2 \times 47 \times 53\)
- Prime factorization of 28: \(28 = 2^2 \times 7\)

The LCM is the product of the highest powers of all prime factors:
\[ \text{LCM}(4982, 28) = 2^2 \times 7 \times 47 \times 53 = 4 \times 7 \times 47 \times 53 \]

Calculating the product:
\[ 4 \times 7 = 28 \]
\[ 28 \times 47 = 1316 \]
\[ 1316 \times 53 = 69748 \]

So, the common denominator is 69748.

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 69748:
\[ \frac{12857}{4982} = \frac{12857 \times 14}{4982 \times 14} = \frac{180398}{69748} \]
\[ \frac{25}{28} = \frac{25 \times 2491}{28 \times 2491} = \frac{62275}{69748} \]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{180398}{69748} + \frac{62275}{69748} = \frac{180398 + 62275}{69748} = \frac{242673}{69748} \]

Finally, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{242673}{69748}\). We check for the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 242673 and 69748. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[ 242673 \div 69748 \approx 3.48 \quad \text{(quotient 3, remainder 33529)} \]
\[ 69748 \div 33529 \approx 2.08 \quad \text{(quotient 2, remainder 2689)} \]
\[ 33529 \div 2689 \approx 12.47 \quad \text{(quotient 12, remainder 1161)} \]
\[ 2689 \div 1161 \approx 2.32 \quad \text{(quotient 2, remainder 367)} \]
\[ 1161 \div 367 \approx 3.16 \quad \text{(quotient 3, remainder 60)} \]
\[ 367 \div 60 \approx 6.12 \quad \text{(quotient 6, remainder 7)} \]
\[ 60 \div 7 \approx 8.57 \quad \text{(quotient 8, remainder 4)} \]
\[ 7 \div 4 = 1.75 \quad \text{(quotient 1, remainder 3)} \]
\[ 4 \div 3 = 1.33 \quad \text{(quotient 1, remainder 1)} \]
\[ 3 \div 1 = 3 \quad \text{(quotient 3, remainder 0)} \]

The GCD is 1, so the fraction \(\frac{242673}{69748}\) is already in its simplest form.

Problem: Calculate the sum of the following expressions: 1) Divide 10 by 5 and add that result to 35 divided by 27. This will give you a value h. 2) Then, add 47 divided by 99 to h. This will give you a value p. What is the value of p?

GPT-4o: 

Let's break down the problem step by step.

1. First, we need to divide 10 by 5:
\[ \frac{10}{5} = 2 \]

2. Next, we need to divide 35 by 27:
\[ \frac{35}{27} \]

3. We add these two results to get \( h \):
\[ h = 2 + \frac{35}{27} \]

4. Now, we need to add 47 divided by 99 to \( h \):
\[ \frac{47}{99} \]

5. So, the value \( p \) is:
\[ p = 2 + \frac{35}{27} + \frac{47}{99} \]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 27 and 99 is 297.

First, convert \(\frac{35}{27}\) to have a denominator of 297:
\[ \frac{35}{27} = \frac{35 \times 11}{27 \times 11} = \frac{385}{297} \]

Next, convert \(\frac{47}{99}\) to have a denominator of 297:
\[ \frac{47}{99} = \frac{47 \times 3}{99 \times 3} = \frac{141}{297} \]

Now, add these fractions:
\[ \frac{385}{297} + \frac{141}{297} = \frac{385 + 141}{297} = \frac{526}{297} \]

Now, add this result to 2:
\[ p = 2 + \frac{526}{297} \]

Convert 2 to a fraction with a denominator of 297:
\[ 2 = \frac{2 \times 297}{297} = \frac{594}{297} \]

Now, add the fractions:
\[ p = \frac{594}{297} + \frac{526}{297} = \frac{594 + 526}{297} = \frac{1120}{297} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{1120}{297}\)

Expected answer: 1120/297

\frac{63 + 63}{41} = \frac{126}{41}
\]

Thus, the total length of both pieces of ribbon together is \( \frac{126}{41} \) yards.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the result of 92/75 + 66/92? Please give your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To find the result of \( \frac{92}{75} + \frac{66}{92} \), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 75 and 92 will be our common denominator.

1. **Find the LCM of 75 and 92:**
   - The prime factorization of 75 is \( 3 \times 5^2 \).
   - The prime factorization of 92 is \( 2^2 \times 23 \).

   The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime that appears in the factorizations:
   - \( 2^2 \) (from 92)
   - \( 3 \) (from 75)
   - \( 5^2 \) (from 75)
   - \( 23 \) (from 92)

   Therefore, the LCM is \( 2^2 \times 3 \times 5^2 \times 23 = 4 \times 3 \times 25 \times 23 = 6900 \).

2. **Convert each fraction to have the common denominator 6900:**
   - For \( \frac{92}{75} \):
     \[
     \frac{92}{75} = \frac{92 \times 92}{75 \times 92} = \frac{8464}{6900}
     \]

   - For \( \frac{66}{92} \):
     \[
     \frac{66}{92} = \frac{66 \times 75}{92 \times 75} = \frac{4950}{6900}
     \]

3. **Add the fractions:**
   \[
   \frac{8464}{6900} + \frac{4950}{6900} = \frac{8464 + 4950}{6900} = \frac{13414}{6900}
   \]

4. **Simplify the fraction:**
   - Find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 13414 and 6900. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
     \[
     \text{GCD}(13414, 6900) = 2
     \]

   - Divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
     \[
     \frac{13414 \div 2}{6900 \div 2} = \frac{6707}{3450}
     \]

Thus, the simplified fraction is \( \frac{6707}{3450} \).

### Answer: \(\frac{6707}{3450}\)

Expected answer: 6707/3450

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the difference between 51/34 and 12/86? Express your answer in its simplest form.

GPT-4o: 

To find the difference between the fractions \( \frac{51}{34} \) and \( \frac{12}{86} \), we first need to express them with a common denominator.

1. **Simplify the fractions if possible:**
   - \( \frac{51}{34} \) is already in its simplest form.
   - \( \frac{12}{86} \) can be simplified by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 2:
     \[
     \frac{12 \div 2}{86 \div 2} = \frac{6}{43}
     \]

2. **Find a common denominator:**
   - The denominators are 34 and 43. The least common multiple (LCM) of 34 and 43 is 34 * 43 = 1462 (since 34 and 43 are coprime).

3. **Convert each fraction to have the common denominator:**
   - For \( \frac{51}{34} \):
     \[
     \frac{51}{34} = \frac{51 \times 43}{34 \times 43} = \frac{2193}{1462}
     \]
   - For \( \frac{6}{43} \):
     \[
     \frac{6}{43} = \frac{6 \times 34}{43 \times 34} = \frac{204}{1462}
     \]

4. **Subtract the fractions:**
   \[
   \frac{2193}{1462} - \frac{204}{1462} = \frac{2193 - 204}{1462} = \frac{1989}{1462}
   \]

5. **Simplify the resulting fraction:**
   - To simplify \( \frac{1989}{1462} \), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1989 and 1462. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
     \[
     1989 \div 1462 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 527)}
     \]
     \[
     1462 \div 527 \approx 2 \quad \text{(remainder 408)}
     \]
     \[
     527 \div 408 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 119)}
     \]
     \[
     408 \div 119 \approx 3 \quad \text{(remainder 51)}
     \]
     \[
     119 \div 51 \approx 2 \quad \text{(remainder 17)}
     \]
     \[
     51 \div 17 \approx 3 \quad \text{(remainder 0)}
     \]
     The GCD is 17.

   - Divide both the numerator and the denominator by 17:
     \[
     \frac{1989 \div 17}{1462 \div 17} = \frac{117}{86}
     \]

6. **Simplify further if possible:**
   - The fraction \( \frac{117}{86} \) can be simplified by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD, which is 1 (since 117 and 86 are coprime).

Thus, the simplest form of the difference is \( \frac{117}{86} \).

### Answer: \(\frac{117}{86}\)

Expected answer: 117/86

Correct? Yes

   \frac{40}{53} \approx 0.7547
   \]

3. Add the two results to find \( s \):
   \[
   s = 4 + \frac{40}{53} \approx 4 + 0.7547 = 4.7547
   \]

Next, we need to find \( b \) by adding \( s \) to itself:
\[
b = s + s = 2s
\]

\[

\]

2. Subtract \( \frac{46}{41} \) from the result obtained in step 1.
3. Simplify the final result.

Let's start with step 1:

First, we need a common denominator to add \( \frac{92}{54} \) and \( \frac{90}{13} \). The least common multiple (LCM) of 54 and 13 is 702.

Convert \( \frac{92}{54} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 702:
\[ \frac{92}{54} = \frac{92 \times 13}{54 \times 13} = \frac{1196}{702} \]

Convert \( \frac{90}{13} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 702:
\[ \frac{90}{13} = \frac{90 \times 54}{13 \times 54} = \frac{4860}{702} \]

Now, add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{1196}{702} + \frac{4860}{702} = \frac{1196 + 4860}{702} = \frac{6056}{702} \]

Next, simplify \( \frac{6056}{702} \):
The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 6056 and 702 is 2.
\[ \frac{6056 \div 2}{702 \div 2} = \frac{3028}{351} \]

Now, we move to step 2:

\[ \frac{3028}{351} = \frac{3028 \times 41}{351 \times 41} = \frac{124148}{14421} \]

Convert \( \frac{46}{41} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 14421:

Finally, simplify \( \frac{108002}{14421} \):
The GCD of 108002 and 14421 is 1 (since they are relatively prime).

Thus, the fraction is already in its simplest form:
\[ \frac{108002}{14421} \]

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the sum of 29/20 and 17/72? Answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \(\frac{29}{20}\) and \(\frac{17}{72}\), we need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 20 and 72 will be our common denominator.

First, we find the prime factorizations of 20 and 72:
- \(20 = 2^2 \times 5\)
- \(72 = 2^3 \times 3^2\)

The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime that appears in the factorizations:
- \(2^3\) (from 72)
- \(3^2\) (from 72)
- \(5\) (from 20)

Thus, the LCM of 20 and 72 is \(2^3 \times 3^2 \times 5 = 8 \times 9 \times 5 = 360\).

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 360:
- \(\frac{29}{20} = \frac{29 \times 18}{20 \times 18} = \frac{522}{360}\)
- \(\frac{17}{72} = \frac{17 \times 5}{72 \times 5} = \frac{85}{360}\)

Now, we add the fractions:
\[
\frac{522}{360} + \frac{85}{360} = \frac{522 + 85}{360} = \frac{607}{360}
\]

The fraction \(\frac{607}{360}\) is already in its simplest form because 607 is a prime number and does not share any common factors with 360.

### Answer: \(\frac{607}{360}\)

Expected answer: 607/360

Correct? Yes

- \(68 = 2^2 \times 17\)

The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime that appears in the factorizations:
- \(2^3\) (from 360)
- \(3^2\) (from 360)
- \(5\) (from 360)
- \(17\) (from 68)

Thus, the LCM of 360 and 68 is \(2^3 \times 3^2 \times 5 \times 17 = 8 \times 9 \times 5 \times 17 = 6120\).

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 6120:
- \(\frac{607}{360} = \frac{607 \times 17}{360 \times 17} = \frac{10319}{6120}\)
- \(\frac{9}{68} = \frac{9 \times 90}{68 \times 90} = \frac{810}{6120}\)

Now, we subtract the fractions:
\[
\frac{10319}{6120} - \frac{810}{6120} = \frac{10319 - 810}{6120} = \frac{9509}{6120}
\]

Finally, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{9509}{6120}\). We need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 9509 and 6120. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
- \(9509 \div 6120 \approx 1\) remainder \(3389\)
- \(6120 \div 3389 \approx 1\) remainder \(2731\)
- \(3389 \div 2731 \approx 1\) remainder \(658\)
- \(2731 \div 658 \approx 4\) remainder \(99\)
- \(658 \div 99 \approx 6\) remainder \(64\)
- \(99 \div 64 \approx 1\) remainder \(35\)
- \(64 \div 35 \approx 1\) remainder \(29\)
- \(35 \div 29 \approx 1\) remainder \(6\)
- \(29 \div 6 \approx 4\) remainder \(5\)
- \(6 \div 5 \approx 1\) remainder \(1\)
- \(5 \div 1 = 5\) remainder \(0\)

The GCD is 1, so the fraction \(\frac{9509}{6120}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{9509}{6120}\)

Expected answer: 9509/6120

Correct? Yes

Problem: Compute ((75 / 66) + (81 / 61)), and give your answer as a fraction reduced to its lowest term.

GPT-4o: 

To compute \(\left(\frac{75}{66}\right) + \left(\frac{81}{61}\right)\), we first need to find a common denominator for the fractions.

The denominators are 66 and 61. Since 66 and 61 are relatively prime (they have no common factors other than 1), their least common multiple (LCM) is simply their product:
\[ 66 \times 61 = 4026 \]

Next, we convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[ \frac{75}{66} = \frac{75 \times 61}{66 \times 61} = \frac{4575}{4026} \]
\[ \frac{81}{61} = \frac{81 \times 66}{61 \times 66} = \frac{5346}{4026} \]

Now, we can add the fractions:
\[ \frac{4575}{4026} + \frac{5346}{4026} = \frac{4575 + 5346}{4026} = \frac{9921}{4026} \]

To reduce this fraction to its lowest terms, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 9921 and 4026. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[ 9921 \div 4026 \approx 2 \quad \text{(remainder 1869)} \]
\[ 4026 \div 1869 \approx 2 \quad \text{(remainder 288)} \]
\[ 1869 \div 288 \approx 6 \quad \text{(remainder 165)} \]
\[ 288 \div 165 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 123)} \]
\[ 165 \div 123 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 42)} \]
\[ 123 \div 42 \approx 2 \quad \text{(remainder 39)} \]
\[ 42 \div 39 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 3)} \]
\[ 39 \div 3 = 13 \quad \text{(remainder 0)} \]

The GCD is 3. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 3:
\[ \frac{9921 \div 3}{4026 \div 3} = \frac{3307}{1342} \]

Problem: Given that Evan has read 51/18 of his novel, and Olivia has read (8/42) after reading the same amount of novel as Evan, how much of the novel has Olivia read in total? Answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

First, let's simplify the fractions given in the problem.

Evan has read \( \frac{51}{18} \) of his novel. We can simplify this fraction by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 51 and 18.

The prime factorization of 51 is \( 3 \times 17 \).
The prime factorization of 18 is \( 2 \times 3^2 \).

The GCD of 51 and 18 is 3. Therefore, we can simplify \( \frac{51}{18} \) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 3:

\[ \frac{51 \div 3}{18 \div 3} = \frac{17}{6} \]

So, Evan has read \( \frac{17}{6} \) of his novel.

Next, Olivia has read \( \frac{8}{42} \) of the novel after reading the same amount as Evan. We can simplify \( \frac{8}{42} \) by finding the GCD of 8 and 42.

The prime factorization of 8 is \( 2^3 \).
The prime factorization of 42 is \( 2 \times 3 \times 7 \).

The GCD of 8 and 42 is 2. Therefore, we can simplify \( \frac{8}{42} \) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 2:

\[ \frac{8 \div 2}{42 \div 2} = \frac{4}{21} \]

So, Olivia has read \( \frac{4}{21} \) of the novel after reading the same amount as Evan.

To find the total amount Olivia has read, we need to add the amount she read initially (same as Evan) and the additional amount:

\[ \frac{17}{6} + \frac{4}{21} \]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 6 and 21 is 42.

Convert each fraction to have a denominator of 42:

\[ \frac{17}{6} = \frac{17 \times 7}{6 \times 7} = \frac{119}{42} \]
\[ \frac{4}{21} = \frac{4 \times 2}{21 \times 2} = \frac{8}{42} \]

Now, add the fractions:

\[ \frac{119}{42} + \frac{8}{42} = \frac{119 + 8}{42} = \frac{127}{42} \]

The fraction \( \frac{127}{42} \) is already in its simplest form because 127 is a prime number and does not share any common factors with 42.

### Answer: \(\frac{127}{42}\)

Expected answer: 127/42

Correct? Yes

Problem: Find the sum of 73/39 and 49/14, and express your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \(\frac{73}{39}\) and \(\frac{49}{14}\), we first need to find a common denominator.

1. Identify the denominators: 39 and 14.
2. Find the least common multiple (LCM) of 39 and 14.

The prime factorization of 39 is \(3 \times 13\).
The prime factorization of 14 is \(2 \times 7\).

The LCM is the product of the highest powers of all prime factors involved:
\[ \text{LCM}(39, 14) = 2 \times 3 \times 7 \times 13 = 546 \]

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 546.

For \(\frac{73}{39}\):
\[ \frac{73}{39} = \frac{73 \times 14}{39 \times 14} = \frac{1022}{546} \]

For \(\frac{49}{14}\):
\[ \frac{49}{14} = \frac{49 \times 39}{14 \times 39} = \frac{1911}{546} \]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{1022}{546} + \frac{1911}{546} = \frac{1022 + 1911}{546} = \frac{2933}{546} \]

Finally, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{2933}{546}\). We need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 2933 and 546.

Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[ 2933 \div 546 \approx 5 \quad \text{(remainder 203)} \]
\[ 546 \div 203 \approx 2 \quad \text{(remainder 140)} \]
\[ 203 \div 140 \approx 1 \quad \text{(remainder 63)} \]
\[ 140 \div 63 \approx 2 \quad \text{(remainder 14)} \]
\[ 63 \div 14 \approx 4 \quad \text{(remainder 7)} \]
\[ 14 \div 7 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 0)} \]

The GCD is 7.

Now, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[ \frac{2933 \div 7}{546 \div 7} = \frac{419}{78} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{419}{78}\)

Expected answer: 419/78

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: What is the sum of 59/52 and 70/32? Please provide your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the fractions \(\frac{59}{52}\) and \(\frac{70}{32}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 52 and 32 will be our common denominator.

First, we find the prime factorizations of 52 and 32:
- \(52 = 2^2 \times 13\)
- \(32 = 2^5\)

The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime that appears in the factorizations:
- The highest power of 2 is \(2^5\)
- The highest power of 13 is \(13\)

Thus, the LCM of 52 and 32 is \(2^5 \times 13 = 32 \times 13 = 416\).

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 416:
- For \(\frac{59}{52}\):
  \[
  \frac{59}{52} = \frac{59 \times 8}{52 \times 8} = \frac{472}{416}
  \]

- For \(\frac{70}{32}\):
  \[
  \frac{70}{32} = \frac{70 \times 13}{32 \times 13} = \frac{910}{416}
  \]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{472}{416} + \frac{910}{416} = \frac{472 + 910}{416} = \frac{1382}{416}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{1382}{416}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1382 and 416. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
- \(1382 \div 416 = 3\) remainder \(134\)
- \(416 \div 134 = 3\) remainder \(14\)
- \(134 \div 14 = 9\) remainder \(8\)
- \(14 \div 8 = 1\) remainder \(6\)
- \(8 \div 6 = 1\) remainder \(2\)
- \(6 \div 2 = 3\) remainder \(0\)

The GCD is 2. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:
\[
\frac{1382 \div 2}{416 \div 2} = \frac{691}{208}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is \(\frac{691}{208}\).

### Answer: \(\frac{691}{208}\)

Expected answer: 691/208

GPT-4o: 

To add the fractions \( \frac{20}{52} \) and \( \frac{75}{82} \), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 52 and 82 can be found by determining their prime factorizations:

- \( 52 = 2^2 \times 13 \)
- \( 82 = 2 \times 41 \)

The LCM is \( 2^2 \times 13 \times 41 = 2132 \).

Next, we convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

\[ \frac{20}{52} = \frac{20 \times 41}{52 \times 41} = \frac{820}{2132} \]
\[ \frac{75}{82} = \frac{75 \times 26}{82 \times 26} = \frac{1950}{2132} \]

Now, we add the two fractions:

\[ \frac{820}{2132} + \frac{1950}{2132} = \frac{820 + 1950}{2132} = \frac{2770}{2132} \]

To simplify \( \frac{2770}{2132} \), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 2770 and 2132. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \( 2770 \div 2132 \) gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 638.
2. \( 2132 \div 638 \) gives a quotient of 3 and a remainder of 218.
3. \( 638 \div 218 \) gives a quotient of 2 and a remainder of 202.
4. \( 218 \div 202 \) gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 16.
5. \( 202 \div 16 \) gives a quotient of 12 and a remainder of 10.
6. \( 16 \div 10 \) gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 6.
7. \( 10 \div 6 \) gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 4.
8. \( 6 \div 4 \) gives a quotient of 1 and a remainder of 2.
9. \( 4 \div 2 \) gives a quotient of 2 and a remainder of 0.

The GCD is 2. Therefore, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:

\[ \frac{2770 \div 2}{2132 \div 2} = \frac{1385}{1066} \]

Thus, the simplified form of \( \frac{20}{52} + \frac{75}{82} \) is \( \frac{1385}{1066} \).

Problem: Calculate the sum of the fractions 12/70 and 84/9. Please provide your answer in simplified form.

GPT-4o: 

To calculate the sum of the fractions \( \frac{12}{70} \) and \( \frac{84}{9} \), we first need to find a common denominator. However, since the denominators 70 and 9 are relatively prime (they have no common factors other than 1), the common denominator will be their product, which is \( 70 \times 9 = 630 \).

Next, we convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

1. Convert \( \frac{12}{70} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 630:
\[
\frac{12}{70} = \frac{12 \times 9}{70 \times 9} = \frac{108}{630}
\]

2. Convert \( \frac{84}{9} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 630:
\[
\frac{84}{9} = \frac{84 \times 70}{9 \times 70} = \frac{5880}{630}
\]

Now, we can add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{108}{630} + \frac{5880}{630} = \frac{108 + 5880}{630} = \frac{5988}{630}
\]

To simplify \( \frac{5988}{630} \), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 5988 and 630. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \( 5988 \div 630 \approx 9 \) (remainder 288)
2. \( 630 \div 288 \approx 2 \) (remainder 54)
3. \( 288 \div 54 \approx 5 \) (remainder 18)
4. \( 54 \div 18 = 3 \) (remainder 0)

The GCD is 18. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 18:
\[
\frac{5988 \div 18}{630 \div 18} = \frac{333}{35}
\]

Thus, the simplified form of the sum is:
\[
\frac{333}{35}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{333}{35}\)

Expected answer: 998/105

Correct? No

GPT-4o:

1. Subtract \( \frac{40}{92} \) from \( \frac{32}{3} \).
2. Double the result.

First, let's simplify \( \frac{40}{92} \):

\[ \frac{40}{92} = \frac{40 \div 4}{92 \div 4} = \frac{10}{23} \]

Now, we need to subtract \( \frac{10}{23} \) from \( \frac{32}{3} \). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 3 and 23 is 69.

Convert both fractions to have the common denominator of 69:

\[ \frac{32}{3} = \frac{32 \times 23}{3 \times 23} = \frac{736}{69} \]
\[ \frac{10}{23} = \frac{10 \times 3}{23 \times 3} = \frac{30}{69} \]

Now, subtract the fractions:

\[ \frac{736}{69} - \frac{30}{69} = \frac{736 - 30}{69} = \frac{706}{69} \]

Next, double the result:

\[ 2 \times \frac{706}{69} = \frac{2 \times 706}{69} = \frac{1412}{69} \]

Simplify the fraction:

\[ \frac{1412}{69} = \frac{1412 \div 1}{69 \div 1} = \frac{1412}{69} \]

Since 1412 and 69 have no common factors other than 1, the fraction is already in its simplest form.

2. Add the result to \( \frac{92}{4} \).

First, let's find a common denominator for \( \frac{88}{93} \) and \( \frac{6}{47} \). The least common multiple (LCM) of 93 and 47 is 4371.

Convert \( \frac{88}{93} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 4371:
\[ \frac{88}{93} = \frac{88 \times 47}{93 \times 47} = \frac{4136}{4371} \]

Convert \( \frac{6}{47} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 4371:
\[ \frac{6}{47} = \frac{6 \times 93}{47 \times 93} = \frac{558}{4371} \]

\[ \frac{4694}{4371} = 1 + \frac{323}{4371} \]

So, we need to add:
\[ 23 + 1 + \frac{323}{4371} = 24 + \frac{323}{4371} \]

Thus, the final result is:
\[ 24 + \frac{323}{4371} \]

Problem: Calculate ((92 / 95) + (4 / 74)). Answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To solve \(\left(\frac{92}{95}\right) + \left(\frac{4}{74}\right)\), we first need to find a common denominator for the fractions.

The denominators are 95 and 74. The least common multiple (LCM) of 95 and 74 can be found by their prime factorizations:
- 95 = 5 Ã— 19
- 74 = 2 Ã— 37

Since 95 and 74 have no common prime factors, their LCM is \(95 \times 74 = 7030\).

Next, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 7030:
\[
\frac{92}{95} = \frac{92 \times 74}{95 \times 74} = \frac{6808}{7030}
\]
\[
\frac{4}{74} = \frac{4 \times 95}{74 \times 95} = \frac{380}{7030}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{6808}{7030} + \frac{380}{7030} = \frac{6808 + 380}{7030} = \frac{7188}{7030}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{7188}{7030}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 7188 and 7030. Using the Euclidean algorithm:
\[
7188 - 7030 = 158
\]
\[
7030 \div 158 = 44.4937 \quad \text{(not an integer, so we continue)}
\]
\[
7030 \mod 158 = 94
\]
\[
158 \div 94 = 1.6809 \quad \text{(not an integer, so we continue)}
\]
\[
158 \mod 94 = 64
\]
\[
94 \div 64 = 1.46875 \quad \text{(not an integer, so we continue)}
\]
\[
94 \mod 64 = 30
\]
\[
64 \div 30 = 2.1333 \quad \text{(not an integer, so we continue)}
\]
\[
64 \mod 30 = 4
\]
\[
30 \div 4 = 7.5 \quad \text{(not an integer, so we continue)}
\]
\[
30 \mod 4 = 2
\]
\[
4 \div 2 = 2 \quad \text{(integer, so we stop)}
\]

The GCD is 2. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:
\[
\frac{7188 \div 2}{7030 \div 2} = \frac{3594}{3515}
\]

Thus, the simplified fraction is:
\[
\frac{3594}{3515}
\]

Problem: Let's say there is a wholesaler who has 41/26 barrels of olive oil in their warehouse. They sell a portion of the oil which is equivalent to 41/72 barrels. How much olive oil do they have now? Express your answer as a simple fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much olive oil the wholesaler has left, we need to subtract the amount sold from the initial amount.

The initial amount of olive oil is \(\frac{41}{26}\) barrels.
The amount sold is \(\frac{41}{72}\) barrels.

First, we need a common denominator to subtract these fractions. The least common multiple (LCM) of 26 and 72 is 936.

Convert \(\frac{41}{26}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 936:
\[
\frac{41}{26} = \frac{41 \times 36}{26 \times 36} = \frac{1476}{936}
\]

Convert \(\frac{41}{72}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 936:
\[
\frac{41}{72} = \frac{41 \times 13}{72 \times 13} = \frac{533}{936}
\]

Now, subtract the two fractions:
\[
\frac{1476}{936} - \frac{533}{936} = \frac{1476 - 533}{936} = \frac{943}{936}
\]

Thus, the wholesaler has \(\frac{943}{936}\) barrels of olive oil left. This fraction can be simplified further by recognizing that both the numerator and the denominator are divisible by 1 (since 943 and 936 have no common factors other than 1).

Problem: What is the result of adding 12 over 33 to 49 over 2? Write your answer as a mixed fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To add the fractions \(\frac{12}{33}\) and \(\frac{49}{2}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 33 and 2 is 66.

1. Convert \(\frac{12}{33}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 66:
\[
\frac{12}{33} = \frac{12 \times 2}{33 \times 2} = \frac{24}{66}
\]

2. Convert \(\frac{49}{2}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 66:
\[
\frac{49}{2} = \frac{49 \times 33}{2 \times 33} = \frac{1617}{66}
\]

3. Add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{24}{66} + \frac{1617}{66} = \frac{24 + 1617}{66} = \frac{1641}{66}
\]

4. Simplify \(\frac{1641}{66}\) if possible. First, we check for the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1641 and 66. The GCD is 3.

\[
\frac{1641 \div 3}{66 \div 3} = \frac{547}{22}
\]

5. Convert \(\frac{547}{22}\) to a mixed fraction:
\[
547 \div 22 = 24 \text{ remainder } 19
\]
So, \(\frac{547}{22} = 24 \frac{19}{22}\).

Problem: What is the result of adding two fractions, where each fraction is 78/65?

GPT-4o: 

To add two fractions, we first ensure they have the same denominator. In this case, both fractions are \(\frac{78}{65}\), so they already have the same denominator.

The sum of the two fractions is:
\[
\frac{78}{65} + \frac{78}{65}
\]

When adding fractions with the same denominator, we add the numerators and keep the denominator the same:
\[
\frac{78 + 78}{65} = \frac{156}{65}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{156}{65}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 156 and 65. The GCD of 156 and 65 is 13.

We divide both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD:
\[
\frac{156 \div 13}{65 \div 13} = \frac{12}{5}
\]

Thus, the simplified result of adding the two fractions is:
\[
\frac{12}{5}
\]

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Calculate the sum of 16/7 and 11/90. Answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To add the fractions \(\frac{16}{7}\) and \(\frac{11}{90}\), we need to find a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 7 and 90 is 630.

First, we convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 630:

\[
\frac{16}{7} = \frac{16 \times 90}{7 \times 90} = \frac{1440}{630}
\]

\[
\frac{11}{90} = \frac{11 \times 7}{90 \times 7} = \frac{77}{630}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:

\[
\frac{1440}{630} + \frac{77}{630} = \frac{1440 + 77}{630} = \frac{1517}{630}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{1517}{630}\). We need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1517 and 630. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

\[
1517 \div 630 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 257)}
\]
\[
630 \div 257 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 116)}
\]
\[
257 \div 116 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 25)}
\]
\[
116 \div 25 = 4 \quad \text{(remainder 16)}
\]
\[
25 \div 16 = 1 \quad \text{(remainder 9)}
\]
\[
16 \div 9 = 1 \quad \text{(remainder 7)}
\]
\[
9 \div 7 = 1 \quad \text{(remainder 2)}
\]
\[
7 \div 2 = 3 \quad \text{(remainder 1)}
\]
\[
2 \div 1 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 0)}
\]

The GCD is 1, so the fraction \(\frac{1517}{630}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{1517}{630}\)

Expected answer: 1517/630

Correct? Yes

GPT-4o:

Next, we need to add \(\frac{1517}{630}\) to \(\frac{38}{69}\). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 630 and 69 is 43470.

\[
\frac{1517}{630} = \frac{1517 \times 69}{630 \times 69} = \frac{104673}{43470}

\[

\]

Now, we add the two fractions:

\[
\frac{104673}{43470} + \frac{23940}{43470} = \frac{104673 + 23940}{43470} = \frac{128613}{43470}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{128613}{43470}\). We need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 128613 and 43470. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

\[
128613 \div 43470 = 2 \quad \text{(remainder 41673)}
\]
\[
43470 \div 41673 = 1 \quad \text{(remainder 1797)}
\]
\[
